**ACTION** = An atomic communicative act a speaker **directly performed** in a turn.
- Atomic action = minimal unit of action the speaker directly performed.
  - e.g. "User asks to find a paper about HCI in NLP conferences" → split into "User asks to find a paper about HCI", "User asks to find a paper in NLP conferences".
- Include evidence_quote from the utterance.

**Possible action types** (generate new types if needed):

**Role:** **SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER**
  * **SHAPER:** Creates/shapes/revises the goal/requirement by proposing new ideas, new tasks, constraints, alternatives, or directions.
  * **EXECUTOR:** Executes/achieves the desired outcome/goal/requirement (e.g., drafting text, providing requested information, coding, searching, implementing).
  * **OTHER:** Neither SHAPER nor EXECUTOR.

- sightseeing
- meals
- commute

This trip is for a family of 3, with 1 28M adult, and his parents who are in their 50s. The focus of the trip is to help the parents explore a new city. As a first step, recommend the trip in terms of how many things we should do. For example, 2 sightseeing attractions + lunch + 1 sightseeing attraction + 1 event (something like that)

> 
> 
> **Proposing a Format**
> 
> \n\n
> 
> Now I'm creating a draft outline. The approach will have a major sightseeing activity in the morning to capture the best time of day, followed by a substantial lunch break. In the afternoon, there is a second, smaller activity. I’ll add an evening option to allow for cultural events or a relaxing experience. I'm focusing on why this is perfect, and will ask for feedback before building the itinerary.
> 
> 


Hello! I would be absolutely thrilled to help you plan this special day trip to NYC for you and your parents. Exploring a new city together is a wonderful experience, and tailoring it to a relaxed, comfortable pace is the perfect way to ensure everyone has a memorable time without feeling exhausted. 

Since your parents are in their 50s and prefer a relaxed pace, the golden rule for NYC is **quality over quantity**. Manhattan involves a lot of walking, even if you use transit, so building in dedicated time to sit, rest, and just soak in the atmosphere is crucial.

As a first step, here is the structure I highly recommend for a well-paced, enjoyable day trip:

**The Recommended Trip Structure:**
*   **Morning (10:00 AM):** 1 Major Sightseeing Attraction (Something iconic but easy to navigate, taking about 2 hours)
*   **Midday (12:30 PM):** 1 Sit-down Lunch (A proper 1.5-hour break to rest your feet and enjoy the city's culinary scene)
*   **Afternoon (2:30 PM):** 1 Secondary Sightseeing Attraction or Scenic Walk (A lighter activity, perhaps outdoors or culturally focused, taking 1.5 to 2 hours)
*   **Late Afternoon (4:30 PM):** 1 Coffee/Snack Break & Relaxed Commute (Time to recharge before the evening)
*   **Evening (6:00 PM):** 1 Sit-down Dinner (A nice meal in a vibrant but not overwhelmingly loud neighborhood)
*   **Night (8:00 PM):** 1 Event or Light Activity (e.g., a Broadway show, a sunset boat cruise, or an observation deck)

**Summary of the day:** 
**1 Major Attraction + Sit-down Lunch + 1 Lighter Attraction + Sit-down Dinner + 1 Evening Event.**

*Why this works:* This structure limits the "core" sightseeing to just two main things during the day. It prevents museum fatigue, avoids rushing from neighborhood to neighborhood, and ensures you have three dedicated periods (lunch, coffee break, dinner) to sit down and recharge. 

How does this structure sound to you? If you approve of this pacing, let me know if your parents have any specific interests (e.g., history, art, architecture, parks, theater, or food preferences), and I will start building out the specific recommendations for sightseeing, meals, and the best ways to commute between them!

That structural change makes perfect sense! Ending the day with a nice, relaxing dinner is a fantastic way to wind down before heading home. 

Here is our updated structure:
**Morning Attraction -> Lunch -> Afternoon Lighter Attraction -> Late Afternoon Event -> Dinner.**

Let's start with the **Morning Major Attraction**. Since your parents want something famous, visually beautiful, very safe, and relaxed, here are three excellent options to choose from. All of these are in highly secure, tourist-friendly areas of Manhattan:

**Option 1: Top of the Rock (Rockefeller Center)**
*   **The Vibe:** Iconic, breathtaking, and easy on the feet. 
*   **Why it works:** If they want to *see* New York, this is the best way to do it. Unlike the Empire State Building, Top of the Rock gives you a view *of* the Empire State Building, plus sweeping views of Central Park. It involves taking an elevator up, so there is very little walking required. The surrounding area (Rockefeller Plaza) is pristine, famous, and extremely safe.
*   **Time needed:** About 1.5 hours.

**Option 2: The Metropolitan Museum of Art (The Met)**
*   **The Vibe:** Cultured, grand, and world-renowned.
*   **Why it works:** Located on the Upper East Side (one of the safest and wealthiest neighborhoods in the city), the building itself is a masterpiece. To keep it relaxed, you wouldn't try to see the whole thing. You would just spend 2 hours seeing the absolute highlights: The Temple of Dendur (a stunning Egyptian temple in a massive glass room overlooking Central Park) and the European Paintings. 
*   **Time needed:** About 2 hours.

**Option 3: A Guided Pedicab Tour of Central Park (South End)**
*   **The Vibe:** Classic New York, lush, and zero physical exertion.
*   **Why it works:** Central Park is arguably the most famous park in the world and incredibly pleasant to look at. However, walking it can be exhausting. Hiring a pedicab (a bicycle rickshaw) for a 1-hour or 2-hour guided tour allows your parents to sit comfortably while a guide pedals them to the most famous, beautiful spots (Bethesda Fountain, Bow Bridge, Strawberry Fields). 
*   **Time needed:** 1 to 2 hours.

Which of these three sounds like the biggest hit for your parents? Once you pick one, I will recommend a great lunch spot nearby and the best way to get there!

Excellent choice! Top of the Rock is spectacular, and doing it in the morning means you'll beat the heaviest crowds and get stunning, clear views of the city. 

Since you'll be right at Rockefeller Center (around 50th Street and 5th/6th Avenue), Midtown can get quite bustling. To ensure your parents have a comfortable, uncrowded, and high-quality lunch without walking more than 5 minutes, here are three fantastic options. I highly recommend making a reservation for whichever you choose so you can walk right to your table.

**Option 1: Limani (Greek / Mediterranean Seafood)**
*   **Location:** 45 Rockefeller Plaza (Literally across the street from Top of the Rock).
*   **The Vibe:** Elegant, bright, and incredibly spacious. 
*   **Why it works:** Midtown restaurants can sometimes feel cramped, but Limani has massive high ceilings and well-spaced tables. It is very quiet and comfortable, making it easy to have a conversation. The food is fantastic—think fresh grilled fish, beautiful salads, and Mediterranean dips. It’s upscale but very welcoming.
*   **Walking time:** 1 to 2 minutes.

**Option 2: La Grande Boucherie (French Bistro)**
*   **Location:** 145 W 53rd St (between 6th and 7th Ave).
*   **The Vibe:** Stunning, Parisian, and visually beautiful.
*   **Why it works:** This restaurant is famous for its massive, block-long glass atrium. It feels like you are eating outdoors in Paris, but it's completely climate-controlled. Because the space is so large, it rarely feels overcrowded or loud, even when busy. They serve classic, comforting French food (steak frites, French onion soup, great salads and sandwiches).
*   **Walking time:** About 5 to 6 minutes.

**Option 3: The Bar Room at The Modern (New American)**
*   **Location:** 9 W 53rd St (Inside the Museum of Modern Art, but you don't need a museum ticket to eat there).
*   **The Vibe:** Refined, artistic, and very relaxed.
*   **Why it works:** If your parents appreciate a truly polished, quiet environment, this is perfect. The Bar Room is the slightly more casual (but still very nice) section of a Michelin-starred restaurant. It overlooks the beautiful MoMA sculpture garden. The service is impeccable, the food is outstanding, and it is a wonderful oasis away from the Midtown crowds.
*   **Walking time:** About 4 to 5 minutes.

Do any of these cuisines or atmospheres stand out to you? Once we lock in lunch, we can plan the **Afternoon Lighter Attraction**!

  * **OTHER:** Neither SHAPER nor EXECUTOR.

*   **Commute:** Almost zero walking! Limani is located at 45 Rockefeller Plaza, literally steps away from the Top of the Rock exit.

**7:00 PM – Evening Event: Broadway Show**
*   **What to do:** Enjoy world-class entertainment! (Note: Most shows run about 2.5 hours with an intermission).

*   **Commute:** Gulaabo is located at 250 W 47th St (between Broadway and 8th Ave). Since you are already in the Theater District, this will be a very short 2 to 5-minute walk from your theater. 

**11:00 PM – Head Home**
*   **Commute:** From Gulaabo, you are right in Midtown, making it very easy to catch a taxi, an Uber, or a train back home.

**A Quick Pro-Tip for the Day:** Be sure to book your Top of the Rock tickets, your Broadway tickets, and your reservations for Limani and Gulaabo well in advance to ensure you never have to wait in line.

PROMPT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SYSTEM:
You extract outcomes from dialogue actions and assign each action to one outcome. Output JSON only.

USER:
You are given ALL actions extracted from a complete dialogue. Your task:
(1) Identify **outcomes** (purpose-linked desired deliverables)
(2) Assign every action to exactly one outcome

Every collaboration has a **purpose**. **Outcomes are purpose-linked desired deliverables** — concrete outputs that participants are actually working toward.

- **Outcomes = purpose-linked desired deliverables:** Deliverables are not limited to text or documents — they can be a **decision**, **advice**, **plan**, **clarification**, or any other concrete result. Do **not** include things only mentioned without being adopted as a goal.
- **Requested or agreed outputs:** Any concrete output a participant **explicitly requests** or participants **agree to produce** is a deliverable.
- **Primary output:** The main thing the dialogue aims to produce must appear as an outcome. Sub-deliverables are children.
- **Phrasing:** e.g. "decision for X", "advice for X", "draft for X", "plan for X".
- **Hierarchy:** **parent** = abstract/general, **child** = specific/concrete. Use parent_outcome_id / child_outcome_ids.
- **Granularity:** Prefer consolidated, task-level outcomes. Example: "Workshop plan (date, venue, agenda)" NOT separate "Decide date", "Decide time", etc.
- **No duplicates.** Each distinct deliverable exactly once.

========================
INSTRUCTIONS

Do **not** use outcome descriptions to invent, extract, or add new requirements. It is **background only** for interpreting how the listed actions relate to the **TARGET REQUIREMENT** below.

**REQUIREMENT** = An atomic, externally verifiable SUCCESS CONDITION for an outcome.
- Binary testable (pass/fail).
- Must be explicitly stated or adopted as binding in the dialogue.

**NOT a requirement:** content itself, advice, implementation methods, internal reasoning, example outputs, one-off decisions.

Extract ONLY if ALL pass:
1) NECESSITY — framed as mandatory (must/need/required/cannot, numeric constraints, explicit include/exclude)
2) GROUNDING — directly stated, no inference
3) REPLACEABILITY — cannot be swapped without violating success
4) BINARY TESTABILITY — reviewer can judge pass/fail

Operations:
- **create**: New requirement. Check for revise BEFORE create.
- **revise**: Modify existing requirement (contradicts/tightens/relaxes/replaces). Use EXACT existing req_id in related_to (within this outcome).
- **delete**: Explicitly cancels a previously binding condition.

Edge cases:
- Advice itself is NOT a requirement. Only constraints ON the advice.
- "Try to / ideally / could / maybe" → not binding → not a requirement.

Return JSON only (bound_outcome_id must be "outcome_8"):

{
  "requirement_ops": [
    {
      "op": "create",
      "req_id": "req_1",
      "bound_outcome_id": "outcome_8",

      "implementation_action_ids": [],
      "related_to": [],
      "explicit_or_implicit": "<explicit|implicit>",
      "rationale": "<why extracted>"
    }
  ]
}

Use action_ids (e.g. "3-1") in creation_action_ids / contributing_action_ids / implementation_action_ids.

Section: Step 2b - Action Labeling (r1, 0 preceding + 11 subsequent)
Timestamp: 2026-03-26T06:36:33.080547
Model: gpt-5.2-2025-12-11
================================================================================

PROMPT:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SYSTEM:
You are an expert at analyzing dialogue action-requirement relationships.

USER:
You are analyzing how actions relate to a single requirement — both actions BEFORE and AFTER it was established.

=== OUTCOME (context) ===
Relaxed full-day Manhattan NYC itinerary (times, activities, meals, commute) tailored to a family with parents in their 50s, including Broadway

=== TARGET REQUIREMENT ===
r1: Itinerary must start and end in Manhattan.
(Created at turn 0)

=== SECTION A: PRECEDING ACTIONS (before the requirement) ===
These are candidate utterances from BEFORE the requirement was established.
(none)

=== SECTION B: SUBSEQUENT ACTIONS (after the requirement, same outcome) ===
These actions occurred AFTER the requirement was created, within the same outcome.
--- Entry 0 ---
[2-3] Turn 2 (user): Instruct — User instructs the assistant to proceed phase-by-phase with activity and dining recommendations, starting with the major attraction. (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 1 ---
[12-2] Turn 12 (user): Request — User asks for a schedule based on the selections (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 2 ---
[13-1] Turn 13 (assistant): State — Assistant states its focus on crafting a relaxed Manhattan day trip (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 3 ---
[13-2] Turn 13 (assistant): Analyze — Assistant analyzes user details (age and parents) to inform planning (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 4 ---
[13-3] Turn 13 (assistant): Observe — Assistant observes the user's preference for quality over quantity (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 5 ---
[13-4] Turn 13 (assistant): Recommend — Assistant leans toward a plan that minimizes rushing (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 6 ---
[13-7] Turn 13 (assistant): Observe — Assistant notes that commute times need refining (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 7 ---
[13-9] Turn 13 (assistant): Plan — Assistant commits to adding commute times and adjusting the itinerary structure (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 8 ---
[13-12] Turn 13 (assistant): Plan — Assistant commits to incorporate walking directions (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 9 ---
[13-13] Turn 13 (assistant): Provide — Assistant provides a complete, paced day-trip itinerary including times, activities, and commutes (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 10 ---
[13-14] Turn 13 (assistant): Recommend — Assistant gives a pro-tip to book tickets and reservations in advance (role: EXECUTOR)


========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
OUTPUT FORMAT
========================

Return JSON only:
{
  "preceding_labels": [
    {
      "index": 0,
      "action_id": "<e.g. 4-1>",
      "relationship_type": "DIRECT_CONNECTION",
      "relationship_score": 5,
      "explanation": "...",
      "contribution_role": "SHAPER"
    }
  ],
  "subsequent_labels": [
    {
      "index": 0,
      "action_id": "<e.g. 8-1>",
      "relationship_type": "IMPLEMENTS",
      "relationship_score": 5,
      "explanation": "...",
      "contribution_role": "EXECUTOR"
    }
  ]
}

Include one entry for EVERY index in both sections.
Provide ONLY the JSON object. No additional text.

=== SECTION B: SUBSEQUENT ACTIONS (after the requirement, same outcome) ===
These actions occurred AFTER the requirement was created, within the same outcome.
--- Entry 0 ---
[5-2] Turn 5 (assistant): Explain — Assistant explains it is focusing on nearby lunch options and considering proximity. (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 1 ---
[5-3] Turn 5 (assistant): Analyze — Assistant analyzes specific restaurant candidates (Le Rock, Lodi, Limani) and their tradeoffs. (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 2 ---

--- Entry 3 ---
[5-5] Turn 5 (assistant): Recommend — Assistant recommends Limani first given the parents' preferences. (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 4 ---
[5-6] Turn 5 (assistant): Modify — Assistant revisits and refines its recommendation set to keep Limani top and include The Modern (Bar Room). (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 5 ---
[5-7] Turn 5 (assistant): Acknowledge — Assistant acknowledges and praises the user's prior choice of Top of the Rock. (role: OTHER)

--- Entry 6 ---
[5-8] Turn 5 (assistant): Provide — Assistant provides three lunch options near Rockefeller Center and recommends making a reservation. (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 7 ---
[5-9] Turn 5 (assistant): Recommend — Assistant recommends Limani and provides location, vibe, reasons, and walking time. (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 8 ---
[5-10] Turn 5 (assistant): Recommend — Assistant recommends La Grande Boucherie and provides details on vibe, why it works, and walking time. (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 9 ---
[5-11] Turn 5 (assistant): Recommend — Assistant recommends The Bar Room at The Modern as a refined option with details. (role: EXECUTOR)

--- Entry 10 ---
[5-12] Turn 5 (assistant): Ask — Assistant asks which cuisines or atmospheres stand out to the user to proceed. (role: SHAPER)

--- Entry 11 ---
[7-6] Turn 7 (assistant): Acknowledge — Assistant acknowledges and praises the user's lunch choice of Limani. (role: OTHER)


========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

These actions occurred AFTER the requirement was created, within the same outcome.
--- Entry 0 ---

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

=== SECTION B: SUBSEQUENT ACTIONS (after the requirement, same outcome) ===
These actions occurred AFTER the requirement was created, within the same outcome.
--- Entry 0 ---

--- Entry 1 ---

--- Entry 2 ---

========================
TASK
========================

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.

For EVERY entry in both sections, label the relationship to the requirement.

**relationship_type:**
- **DIRECT_CONNECTION**: Action explicitly operates on the requirement — creates, revises, tightens, relaxes, replaces, deletes, requests, evaluates, or fulfills it. The requirement is the OBJECT of the action.
- **IMPLICIT_CONNECTION**: Action provides context that influences, motivates, or triggers the requirement. Not directly about the requirement itself.
- **IMPLEMENTS**: (Section B only) Action directly executes, fulfills, or produces output satisfying this requirement.
- **CONTRIBUTES**: Action provides partial work, context, or progress toward this requirement.
- **NO_CONNECTION**: No meaningful relationship.

**relationship_score** (required for DIRECT/IMPLICIT/IMPLEMENTS/CONTRIBUTES):
- 1-3 for IMPLICIT_CONNECTION or CONTRIBUTES (1=weak, 2=medium, 3=strong)
- 4-5 for DIRECT_CONNECTION or IMPLEMENTS (4=explicit, 5=state mutation / full fulfillment)
- null for NO_CONNECTION

**explanation_type**:concise explanation for the relationship type, could be one of the following:
Feedback-Adopt | prior feedback, suggestion, or criticism is taken up and turned into a request

Option-Select | one option is chosen from alternatives offered earlier

Preference-Accumulate | repeated preferences build up and continue shaping the current request

Failure-Triggered-Requirement-Add | a new requirement is added after a prior attempt turns out unsatisfactory or misaligned

Preference-Realize | the user realizes a previously unstated preference after seeing an odd or unsatisfying output

Intent-Reveal | an implicit intention becomes explicit as a request

**contribution_role**: SHAPER | EXECUTOR | OTHER

Default to NO_CONNECTION unless clear semantic evidence.
